## Section 001: Plugin Hook Development Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without its governing split, hookify rules are user-local markdown files matched by regex while plugin hooks are hooks.json event handlers, and prompt-based hooks are the recommended default over command hooks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because hook-development states focus on prompt-based hooks for most use cases and reserve command hooks for performance-critical or deterministic checks, while hookify stores rules in .claude/hookify.{rule-name}.local.md files
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: conflating the two systems sends a user editing hooks.json when a one-file hookify rule would do, or shipping a personal hookify rule where a plugin hook was needed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference operationalizes the hookify rule format and the plugin hook lifecycle across its nine events, not Claude Code plugin development at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open with the two-system split, the nine hook events, and the prompt-over-command default with its deterministic-check exception
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that both systems converge on the same design pressure, validation logic wants to live in natural language, hookify puts the message body in markdown and hook-development migrates regex scripts into prompt criteria
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to reach for a hookify rule for personal per-project guardrails and a plugin hooks.json entry for distributable event automation, with prompt hooks unless the check is deterministic
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because hook-development states focus on prompt-based hooks for most use cases and reserve command hooks for performance-critical or deterministic checks, while hookify stores rules in .claude/hookify.{rule-name}.local.md files
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; conflating the two systems sends a user editing hooks.json when a one-file hookify rule would do, or shipping a personal hookify rule where a plugin hook was needed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference operationalizes the hookify rule format and the plugin hook lifecycle across its nine events, not Claude Code plugin development at large
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open with the two-system split, the nine hook events, and the prompt-over-command default with its deterministic-check exception
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies both systems converge on the same design pressure, validation logic wants to live in natural language, hookify puts the message body in markdown and hook-development migrates regex scripts into prompt criteria

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the wrong-choice boundary is concrete: conflating the two systems sends a user editing hooks.json when a one-file hookify rule would do, or shipping a personal hookify rule where a plugin hook was needed
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Plugin Hook Development Patterns", Question 04 on failure boundary: the boundary is important because the main risks are hooks load at session start and cannot be hot-swapped, editing hooks.json mid-session silently changes nothing until restart

## Section 003: Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scoreboard scores corpus hygiene while the corpus's load-bearing hook rules go unranked, prompt hooks over regex scripts, ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT} for every path, parallel-safe independent hooks, and restart-to-reload awareness
- **supporting_reason:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because each rule guards a distinct failure, regex scripts miss variants, hardcoded paths break portability, order-dependent hooks race, and stale sessions run yesterday's hooks
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the seed's numeric scores were never measured and the corpus offers only a recommended-versus-reserved ordering, not numbers
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scoreboard ranks hook-discipline rules for adoption priority and does not rank the nine events against each other
- **revision_decision:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to promote a top tier of four rules, prefer prompt hooks for complex logic, reference all files through ${CLAUDE_PLUGIN_ROOT}, design hooks to run independently because matching hooks execute in parallel, and restart the session after any hook change

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed thesis repeats the load-local-first formula instead of the corpus's claim, that event-time guardrails should be expressed as natural-language criteria evaluated by prompt hooks, with command hooks reserved for deterministic speed
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because migration.md argues the conversion case end to end, regex catches literal strings while prompts understand intent, and hook-development's closing line makes prompt-first the official stance
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a thesis built on command-hook mechanics alone would canonize the exact style the corpus spends a whole reference file migrating away from
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the thesis orients use of this reference and does not compress the per-event rules it stands on
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to restate the combined inference as express guardrails in natural language where reasoning helps, keep bash where determinism and latency rule, and make every hook portable, parallel-safe, and restart-aware
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the migration is really a trust shift, from trusting the pattern author to enumerate every dangerous string to trusting the model to recognize the category, which is why hybrid multi-stage validation keeps both layers
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to phrase the thesis as prompt-first with a deterministic exception, with the three evidence labels kept on its clauses
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because migration.md argues the conversion case end to end, regex catches literal strings while prompts understand intent, and hook-development's closing line makes prompt-first the official stance

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says use this reference when the theme matches but not the corpus's own selection logic, event choice by lifecycle moment, hook type by determinism, and system choice by distribution need
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the events-summary table pairs each of nine events with its use, validation before tools, feedback after, completeness at stop, context at session start, and the migration guide pairs hook types with check character
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an agent skipping the three questions defaults to PreToolUse command hooks for everything, the exact posture the corpus migrates away from
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes hook-construction decisions and does not route plugin-versus-MCP architecture choices
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the three-question routine, which lifecycle moment, deterministic or judgment-based, personal or distributable, then map answers to event, type, and system
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the questions are ordered by irreversibility, a wrong event silently never fires, a wrong type merely costs latency or accuracy, and a wrong system just costs a port later
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide routes hook-construction decisions and does not route plugin-versus-MCP architecture choices
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add the three-question routine, which lifecycle moment, deterministic or judgment-based, personal or distributable, then map answers to event, type, and system

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed scenario names a platform builder abstractly while the corpus implies a concrete journey, a builder who saw a dangerous operation slip through and wants event-time enforcement without breaking the team's flow
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because patterns.md opens with exactly these journeys, block dangerous writes, enforce tests before stopping, load context at session start, each a response to a felt incident
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without the incident framing the scenario cannot explain the corpus's insistence on warn-versus-block and ask-decisions, escalation levels only matter to someone weighing friction against safety
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the scenario motivates this reference and does not prescribe one pattern for all teams
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to recast the journey in three acts, incident and desired guardrail, selection via the three routing questions, then implementation with schema validation, sample-input tests, and a debug-mode session
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the journey's real fork is escalation choice, hookify defaults to warn, PreToolUse offers allow, deny, and ask, and pattern 7 shows ask as the middle path that confirms rather than blocks

- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to start new guardrails at warn or ask severity and promote to block only after false-positive review

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide's adopt-adapt-avoid rows never name the corpus's live tradeoffs, prompt accuracy versus command latency, block safety versus warn friction, and hookify speed versus plugin distribution
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because migration.md prices the first tradeoff, prompts understand intent but cost 15-30 second timeouts against sub-50ms regex checks, and the action field prices the second, block prevents while warn merely shows
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a builder using only the seed's generic rows gets no help choosing between a 10ms allowlist and a 15s reasoning pass on every bash call
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide arbitrates hook-construction tradeoffs, not whether event automation is worth having at all
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add three concrete rows, type choice by check character and latency budget, severity choice by false-positive cost, and system choice by who must receive the guardrail
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the hybrid pattern dissolves the first tradeoff instead of picking a side, a quick command check approves the obvious and the prompt hook reasons about the rest, paying latency only on ambiguous cases
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

- **revision_decision:** Section 013 "Theme Specific Artifact", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the artifact as a seven-field row per hook, event, matcher, type, timeout, output contract, escalation level, and test evidence from the three-layer kit

## Section 015: Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed metrics name install-and-debug ease while the corpus implies hook-specific signals, false-positive rate per guardrail, hook timeout frequency, and time from incident to shipped rule
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the escalation ladder from warn to ask to block only functions if someone counts wrong triggers, and the timeout defaults only protect flow if exceedances are noticed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a guardrail with unmeasured false positives drifts to either ignored warnings or resented blocks, and either way the incident it guards recurs
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the metrics govern shipped hooks in use, construction-time checks live in the verification gate
- **revision_decision:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add three loops, sample triggered hooks weekly for false positives before any block promotion, alert on repeated hook timeouts, and track incident-to-rule lead time as the system's responsiveness
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hookify makes the first loop nearly free, toggling enabled false parks a noisy rule without deleting its logic, so the cost of measuring is a frontmatter edit
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to review each guardrail's trigger log before promoting severity and after any prompt-criteria edit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 015 "Outcome Metrics and Feedback Loops", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the escalation ladder from warn to ask to block only functions if someone counts wrong triggers, and the timeout defaults only protect flow if exceedances are noticed

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist audits document sections while a hook is complete only when its event, matcher, type, output schema, tests, and restart step are all in place
- **supporting_reason:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the implementation workflow enumerates nine steps ending in schema validation, sample-input tests, debug-mode verification, and README documentation
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a hook passing the seed's document checks can still ship with an output schema from the wrong event family and fail silently at runtime
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist gates individual hook completion, plugin-wide review aggregates it per hooks.json entry
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to append seven hook items, event matches lifecycle intent, matcher case-sensitivity checked, type justified against the determinism rule, output schema matches the event family, variables quoted and paths portable, all three verification layers run, and session restarted before live testing
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the checklist doubles as the debugging script in reverse, when a hook misbehaves, walking the same items top-down localizes the fault, wrong event, wrong matcher, wrong schema, in that order
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to run the extended checklist on every new hook and after any edit to matcher, prompt, or script

## Section 017: Adjacent Reference Routing
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed routing names plugin, hook, and development neighbors without the boundaries the corpus itself draws, hookify for user-local rules, plugin surfaces for commands and MCP, and settings files for direct user hooks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because hook-development distinguishes plugin hooks.json format from settings format explicitly, and hookify positions its rules as needing no plugin at all
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a task about a personal .claude settings hook routed into plugin-format guidance yields a wrapper-object mismatch that fails to load
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the routing covers surfaces adjacent to hook construction, not the whole extension taxonomy
- **revision_decision:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to route by three tests, personal-versus-distributed to hookify or plugins, event-driven-versus-invoked to hooks or commands, and in-session-versus-external-context to hooks or MCP references
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the seed map's MCP URLs make sense here rather than in evidence, MCP is this theme's most confusable neighbor because both wire external behavior into the session, hooks react to events while MCP serves tools and resources
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 017 "Adjacent Reference Routing", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to apply the three tests before opening this reference, and exit to the matching neighbor on the first mismatch

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds generic sessions while hook workloads have their own axes, events fire on every matching tool call, all matching hooks run in parallel, and each hook holds a private timeout budget
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the parallel-execution section shows three hooks on one Write matcher running simultaneously, and the optimization guidance orders quick deterministic checks before expensive reasoning
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a session with chatty matchers like * on PreToolUse multiplies every tool call by the full hook set, and one slow hook throttles everything it matches
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds per-session hook execution, plugin distribution scale is out of frame
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to model the workload as matcher hit rate times hook cost, with command hooks budgeted in milliseconds, prompt hooks in tens of seconds, and totals reviewed per event
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that matcher specificity is the cheapest capacity lever, narrowing Write|Edit to a file-type condition cuts invocations without touching any hook body, which is why hookify's condition lists exist
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to narrow matchers first, order hybrid stages cheap-to-expensive, and cap prompt hooks on high-frequency events
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the parallel-execution section shows three hooks on one Write matcher running simultaneously, and the optimization guidance orders quick deterministic checks before expensive reasoning

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the model bounds per-session hook execution, plugin distribution scale is out of frame
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: model the workload as matcher hit rate times hook cost, with command hooks budgeted in milliseconds, prompt hooks in tens of seconds, and totals reviewed per event

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed targets track document hygiene while hook reliability has sharper contracts, valid JSON out of every hook, correct exit-code semantics, graceful handling of missing input, and zero secret leakage into logs
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the output-format section fixes the contract, exit 0 shows stdout, exit 2 feeds stderr back to Claude, other codes are non-blocking, and the DONT list bans logging sensitive information
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a hook emitting malformed JSON or the wrong exit code degrades into noise, its verdicts silently ignored while its author believes the guardrail stands
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the targets bind individual hook executions, plugin-level reliability aggregates them
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to set four targets, every execution path emits jq-parseable output, exit codes match the documented semantics, hostile or missing input yields a graceful skip not a crash, and no secret ever reaches transcript or audit log
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that exit 2 is the only blocking signal, so reliability is asymmetric, a crash with code 1 fails open and lets the operation through, meaning defensive hooks must treat their own errors as approvals they never intended
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to test all four targets with sample and hostile inputs before shipping, and re-test after any script edit
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the output-format section fixes the contract, exit 0 shows stdout, exit 2 feeds stderr back to Claude, other codes are non-blocking, and the DONT list bans logging sensitive information
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; a hook emitting malformed JSON or the wrong exit code degrades into noise, its verdicts silently ignored while its author believes the guardrail stands
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the targets bind individual hook executions, plugin-level reliability aggregates them
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: set four targets, every execution path emits jq-parseable output, exit codes match the documented semantics, hostile or missing input yields a graceful skip not a crash, and no secret ever reaches transcript or audit log
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies exit 2 is the only blocking signal, so reliability is asymmetric, a crash with code 1 fails open and lets the operation through, meaning defensive hooks must treat their own errors as approvals they never intended
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: command hooks under test, prompt-hook reliability rests on the runtime honoring its decision schema

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed table lists corpus-drift failures while the corpus documents runtime hook failures, hooks not firing after config edits, matcher typos silently matching nothing, timeouts killing slow validators, and parallel hooks racing on shared temp files
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the lifecycle section states hooks cannot be hot-swapped and require restart, the matcher notes state case sensitivity, and the pitfalls section shows $$-keyed state failing across parallel processes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: each documented mode is silent, no error surfaces when an edited hooks.json is stale or a lowercase matcher never fires, so the guardrail's absence is discovered only by the incident it missed
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table catalogs runtime and configuration failures of hooks themselves, document-generation failures stay in the seed rows
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add four rows, stale-session config with restart as mitigation, dead matcher with /hooks inspection as detection, timeout kill with budget review, and state races with independence redesign
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the shared property of all four is silence, which elevates claude --debug and /hooks from conveniences to the only instruments that make these failures observable at all

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guidance covers corpus-refresh retries while hooks need their own policy, a denied operation is a verdict to respect, a timeout is a budget signal, and rate limiting is a pattern hooks themselves can implement
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because advanced.md ships a rate-limiting hook denying after ten commands per minute, and the timeout defaults define when the runtime abandons a hook rather than waiting
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an agent retrying a deny verbatim converts a working guardrail into a loop, and raising timeouts to accommodate slow hooks trades the whole session's latency for one check
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guidance governs behavior around hook verdicts and budgets, not network retries inside hook scripts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add three rules, treat deny as terminal until the input genuinely changes, treat repeated timeouts as a redesign signal toward hybrid staging or caching, and implement frequency caps as hooks when runaway operations are the risk
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hooks invert the usual retry frame, they are the backpressure mechanism, the rate-limiting pattern shows the guardrail side deliberately pushing back on the agent rather than the agent retrying past it
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to one modified retry after a deny with changed input, zero verbatim retries, and caching before timeout raises
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because advanced.md ships a rate-limiting hook denying after ten commands per minute, and the timeout defaults define when the runtime abandons a hook rather than waiting
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; an agent retrying a deny verbatim converts a working guardrail into a loop, and raising timeouts to accommodate slow hooks trades the whole session's latency for one check
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guidance governs behavior around hook verdicts and budgets, not network retries inside hook scripts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: add three rules, treat deny as terminal until the input genuinely changes, treat repeated timeouts as a redesign signal toward hybrid staging or caching, and implement frequency caps as hooks when runaway operations are the risk
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies hooks invert the usual retry frame, they are the backpressure mechanism, the rate-limiting pattern shows the guardrail side deliberately pushing back on the agent rather than the agent retrying past it
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: deny reasons are informative, a bare deny without explanation invites blind retry and should itself be fixed
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because advanced.md ships a rate-limiting hook denying after ten commands per minute, and the timeout defaults define when the runtime abandons a hook rather than waiting
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the success case ends where an agent retrying a deny verbatim converts a working guardrail into a loop, and raising timeouts to accommodate slow hooks trades the whole session's latency for one check
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: treat these operating conditions as bounded by the guidance governs behavior around hook verdicts and budgets, not network retries inside hook scripts
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: add an explicit use-when statement grounded in deny reasons are informative, a bare deny without explanation invites blind retry and should itself be fixed

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed checklist logs corpus-session facts while hook observability has named instruments, claude --debug for registration and timing, /hooks for the loaded set, audit-log hooks for durable trails, and systemMessage for in-transcript explanation
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the debugging section says to look for hook registration, execution logs, input-output JSON, and timing information under debug mode, and the audit pattern appends timestamp, user, tool, and input per event
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: without these instruments the failure-mode table's silent modes stay invisible, an unregistered hook and a never-matching matcher look identical to absence of events
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the checklist observes hooks in operation, construction-time verification lives in the gate section
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add four items, capture debug output on every release probe, snapshot /hooks after each restart, run an audit-log hook where accountability matters, and have deny paths explain themselves via systemMessage
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that suppressOutput and systemMessage make observability a designed property per hook, each hook chooses what the transcript shows, so silent hooks are a choice that should be deliberate rather than a default
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to verbose systemMessage on deny and ask paths, quiet approvals, and durable audit lines for destructive-operation matchers

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed method demands latency packets generically while hook performance has two documented levers with numbers, timeout ceilings of 60 seconds for command and 30 for prompt hooks, and a five-minute result cache shown in advanced.md
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the optimization guidance orders the method, use command hooks for quick deterministic checks, prompt hooks for complex reasoning, cache validation results in temp files, and minimize I/O in hot paths
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an unverified hook stack degrades every gated tool call, and because hooks run before the tool, users experience the cost as global session sluggishness with no obvious culprit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the method verifies hook execution cost, model-side prompt evaluation cost is observable only as wall-clock
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to define the packet as per-hook wall-clock under debug timing, matcher hit counts per session, cache hit rate where caching exists, and timeout-exceedance count as the hard failure line
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the deepest lever is architectural rather than tunable, the hybrid pattern converts p99 pain into a two-tier cost curve where the cheap tier absorbs the common case and the expensive tier prices only ambiguity
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to measure under debug before and after any hook addition on PreToolUse or file-event matchers, the highest-frequency surfaces
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the optimization guidance orders the method, use command hooks for quick deterministic checks, prompt hooks for complex reasoning, cache validation results in temp files, and minimize I/O in hot paths
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; an unverified hook stack degrades every gated tool call, and because hooks run before the tool, users experience the cost as global session sluggishness with no obvious culprit
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the method verifies hook execution cost, model-side prompt evaluation cost is observable only as wall-clock
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: define the packet as per-hook wall-clock under debug timing, matcher hit counts per session, cache hit rate where caching exists, and timeout-exceedance count as the hard failure line
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the deepest lever is architectural rather than tunable, the hybrid pattern converts p99 pain into a two-tier cost curve where the cheap tier absorbs the common case and the expensive tier prices only ambiguity
### Question 03: When does the default work well?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: the default works well under these conditions: debug timing output is available, otherwise bracket hook cost by toggling the plugin and comparing session feel
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 03 on successful operating conditions: those conditions support the recommendation because the optimization guidance orders the method, use command hooks for quick deterministic checks, prompt hooks for complex reasoning, cache validation results in temp files, and minimize I/O in hot paths

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement bounds corpus generation while hook machinery has its own edges, per-session parallel execution with no cross-hook state, restart-bound configuration, and a single hooks.json per plugin merged with user hooks
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the corpus states plugin hooks merge with user hooks and run in parallel, state sharing works only across sequential events, and configuration loads once per session
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: past these edges the pitfalls arrive, cross-hook temp-file protocols race, per-session counters reset invisibly, and fleet-wide policy pushed through personal hookify files fragments per machine
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the boundary statement marks where hook-level design stops sufficing, not where automation itself should stop
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state three edges, coordination beyond one event sequence needs external state with real locking, policy beyond one user needs plugin distribution rather than hookify convention, and enforcement beyond the session needs CI or server-side controls hooks cannot provide
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hooks are a session-scoped enforcement plane, everything they know dies at session end unless a hook exports it, which is why SessionEnd cleanup and audit exports appear in the corpus as the bridge to durable systems
